## Domain Knowledge
**Domain**: chemical reaction kinetics
**Analysis**: This task involves determining the rate law for a chemical reaction, where dA/dt represents the reaction rate as a function of concentration A and possibly time t. Classical kinetics dictates that reaction rates follow power-law, rational, or more complex functional forms of concentration.

**Common formula structures** (built-in generic + LLM domain-specific):
- Arrhenius equation: k = c0 * exp(c1 / T) (chemical reaction rate dependence on temperature)
- Coulomb's / Newton's inverse-square law: F = c0 / r**2 (gravitational or electrostatic force)
- Stefan-Boltzmann law: P = c0 * T**4 (blackbody radiation power vs temperature)
- Beer-Lambert law: I = c0 * exp(c1 * x) (light intensity attenuation through a medium)
- Michaelis-Menten kinetics: v = c0 * S / (S + c1) (enzyme-catalyzed reaction saturation)
- Hill equation: y = c0 * x**c1 / (x**c1 + c2) (cooperative binding, sigmoidal dose-response)
- Kepler's third law: T**2 = c0 * a**3 (orbital period vs semi-major axis)
- Newton's law of cooling: T = c0 + c1 * exp(c2 * t) (exponential thermal relaxation)
- Clausius-Clapeyron relation: log(P) = c0 + c1 / T (vapor pressure vs temperature)
- Langmuir adsorption isotherm: theta = c0 * P / (1 + c1 * P) (surface adsorption equilibrium)
- Freundlich isotherm: q = c0 * C**c1 (empirical adsorption on heterogeneous surface)
- Stokes' drag: F = c0 * r * v (viscous drag force on a sphere in fluid)
- Logistic growth: N = c0 / (1 + c1 * exp(c2 * t)) (population dynamics with carrying capacity)
- Planck-Wien approximation: I = c0 * f**3 * exp(c1 * f / T) (thermal radiation spectrum)
- Zero-order kinetics: dA_dt = c0 (rate independent of concentration)
- First-order kinetics: dA_dt = c0 * A (rate proportional to concentration)
- Second-order kinetics: dA_dt = c0 * A**2 (rate proportional to square of concentration)
- nth-order kinetics: dA_dt = c0 * A**c1 (general power-law rate dependence)
- Reversible first-order: dA_dt = c0 * A + c1 (forward and reverse reactions with equilibrium)
- Mixed-order kinetics: dA_dt = c0 * A + c1 * A**2 (competing first and second order pathways)
- Autocatalytic reaction: dA_dt = c0 * A * (c1 - A) (product catalyzes its own formation from A)
- Substrate inhibition kinetics: dA_dt = c0 * A / (c1 + A + c2 * A**2) (inhibition at high concentration)
- Second-order with equilibrium: dA_dt = c0 * A**2 + c1 * A + c2 (quadratic rate expression)
- Time-dependent rate: dA_dt = c0 * A * exp(c1 * t) (rate constant changing with time, e.g., photochemical)
- Parallel pathway kinetics: dA_dt = c0 * A**c1 + c2 * A**c3 (multiple simultaneous reaction pathways)
- Fractional order with offset: dA_dt = c0 * A**c1 + c2 (fractional order kinetics with constant source/sink)
- Cooperative kinetics: dA_dt = c0 * A**c1 / (A**c1 + c2) (cooperative concentration dependence)
- Damped rate: dA_dt = c0 * A / (c1 + A) (saturation in rate at high concentration)

**Formula structure heuristic features**:
- Oscillation damping envelope → Exponential decay envelope f(x)*exp(-c*Abs(x)) for symmetric damped oscillation, Gaussian envelope f(x)*exp(-c*x**2) for localized wave packets
- Saturation/clipping effects → Rational fraction x/(1+x), tanh; for variables with alternating positive/negative in oscillatory systems, selectively apply Abs
- Growth/decay → Exponential growth exp(c*t), Logistic 1/(1+exp(-c*x)), power law x**c
- Threshold/activation behavior → Max(x-c, 0), piecewise functions
- Coupling/cross effects → Product terms between variables x*y, power-law coupling x**c1 * y**c2
- Simple power-law concentration dependence → dA_dt = c0 * A**n indicates an nth-order elementary or pseudo-elementary reaction
- Linear dependence on A with nonzero intercept → reversible reaction approaching equilibrium or constant source term
- Rational function of A (numerator/denominator polynomials) → enzyme-like or surface-catalyzed mechanism with intermediate complex formation
- Quadratic or higher polynomial in A → multiple reaction pathways or bimolecular steps involving the same species
- Rate depending on product (c1 - A) → autocatalytic mechanism or approach to equilibrium with stoichiometric constraint
- Explicit time dependence in rate → non-autonomous system such as photolysis with varying light, temperature ramp, or catalyst deactivation
- Negative dA_dt proportional to A → consumption/decay of reactant (standard disappearance kinetics)
- A**2 term dominating at high concentration → bimolecular self-reaction mechanism (dimerization)
